Mr. Presiding Member, I also want to refer to anotherincident. May I know how many more minutes I have got?

ÄìÈåÌ¾åÇç· Ä¾àºòéºëÄå(¶Î¾Îº ¶Ç+ÆÐºÆ §Þ¹Æ¸¼Æ £Á¼Æ¯¿Æ)(The Presiding Member)

You have 15 minutes.

ªÇæ ÇÉêÏà Í¨ù ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ½Á[¹Æ Ä¯Æ¯ÉºÆ)(The Hon. Rauff Hakeem)Thank you.

Sir, may I at this point refer to a serious injustice thatwas caused to the Muslim community of the NorthernProvince way back in 1990. In fact, on the last 23rd of

October, a 100,000 strong IDPs, internally displaced Muslimpopulation of the Northern Province, completed 17 yearsof miserable life in very substandard, squalid conditionsin refugee camps. This is nothing - though it is beingdescribed as ethnic cleansing - but according tointernational conventions a grievous violation of the rightsof the Muslims which tantamount to genocide of the entireMuslim population.

The precarious life with a sense of abysmal insecurityabout their future that these people are subjected to, was atheme of an awareness campaign that was launched in theUnited Kingdom on the 27th of last month and going upto the 7th of November, that is today. I was fortunate enoughto be invited to participate in this awareness campaign whichsought to sensitize the British society about the serioushuman rights violations that had been committed againstthis unfortunate, hapless community, the plight of whomhas virtually been ignored for several years.

I do not for a moment say that no steps have been takento look at the issues of resettlement and rehabilitation ofthis community. As a matter of fact, my party and my formerparty Leader himeself undertook several schemes to see thattheir plight is addressed in the best possible sense. Buthowever, it remains to be addressed fully to see that theyultimately are ensured their right to return to their originalareas of habitation. With that in mind, not with an intentionto seek retribution but with an intention to achieve a healthyreconciliation process, we focused on creating an awarenessamong several members of the international community andwe thought it proper to start from the United Kingdom andI must thank the Sri Lanka Islamic Forum which facilitatedseveral meetings in London. I must thank some Membersof the House of Commons who participated in an awarenessmeeting that was held in a committee room in the House ofCommons and I must particularly thank the four British MPsled by Mr. Andy Love who also happens to be the Chair ofthe Sri Lanka Caucus in the House of Commons, Miss FionaMactaggart, Miss Laura Moffat and Mr. Martin Salter whoparticipated at the meeting and shared their observationsregarding possible steps that they and their party as wellas the Government could take in order to address thegrievances of these unfortunate victims of war.

We also incidentally, Sir, had several other meetings. Onesuch meeting was facilitated by the Sri Lankan HighCommision at the High Commission itself where we wereable to meet with representatives of different shades ofpolitical opinion who were among the diaspora of the SriLankan community representing the Sinhala, the Tamils andthe Muslims.

Then, again we had another meeting at the ChathamHouse where certain policy makers and representatives ofthink tanks in Britain as well as members of humanitarianagencies participated in a very healthy dialogue about theresettlement and rehabilitation including compensationissues relating to the Northern Muslims.

ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ29172918

[ªÇæ ÇÉêÏà Í¨ù ÄÍºå]Having said that, Sir, I must say here that the linkagebetween transitional justice and development is a verypertinent issue which we will have to address in our questfor peace. This, I believe, was experimented by us,particularly the latter. The development part wasexperimented by us at the cost of the former, that is theissue of transitional justice. We have unfortunately paid avery heavy price for this type of approach to this entireissue. To many, these two themes would appear to be widelydesperate. But development seems to be on an entirelydifferent plane in addressing the questions of transitionaljustice which in its current usage means the effectivedelivery of justice to societies in transition from conflictto post-conflict. But some thinkers see that the two as beinginextricably linked. What is the purpose of our developmentefforts, if the very targets of those efforts are not affordedgenuine heeling in terms of their loss? Can there be actualdevelopment without addressing their demands for justice?This was precisely what the Northern Muslims who had beenforcibly evicted from the North way back in 1990 areasking the Government and the international community.It is with that objective in mind that we set about creatingand awareness campaign and successfully launched it inLondon. I must once again thank our Colleagues in theHouse of Commons and particularly to those MP s and someof those others who promised to get involved in thiscampaign in the coming years. This particular issue of theunfortunate victims of war is being pushed to the marginsby deliberate stonewalling by the LTTE, to some extentassisted by the Government also in refusing to recognizethe separate dimension of the Muslims in the peace processand therefore, it is my fervent hope that the Government,the LTTE, and the international community would, at leastat this late stage where it appears that a fertile ground forradicalization is being created among the Muslims as aresult of this neglect would change their policy andapproach towards the accommodation of Muslims in thepeace process.

Thank you very much.

ªÇæ ¦. ¦. ¦. ÄêÌàºåÀå ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ©ºÆ° ©ºÆ° ©ºÆ° ÛÃÆ¶¹Ç)(The Hon. M. M. M. Musthaffa)

“Bismillahir Rahmanir Raheem”

Mr. Presiding Member, it is my privilege to participate inthis Emergency debate today. I take this opportunity to talkabout certain practical difficulties and inconveniences caused

to the people of this country. As you know, kidnappings,extortions and all that are taking place in Colombo and otherareas. I understand that an eight member committee has beenappointed by the Government to look into this. I hope thatproblem would be dealt with by them. I salute my good Friendthe Hon. Mano Ganesan and other people who are veryactively taking action on behalf of the people, especially theTamil people who are affected by this.

On the other hand, Hon. Minister, I would like to bring toyour notice a problem especially the Eastern Province peoplehave to face. The vehicle owners of the Eastern Provincehave to obtain passes. We do not say it should not be done.we do understand the difficulties our security forces have toface due to the number of bombs and dangerous materialCarring in vehicles. But of course Sir, what I appeal to you isthat when there is clear evidence of ownership of a vehicle,those owners could be issued with passes once and for all.This is a practical problem in our area. A person has to stay inthe queue for three, four or five hours at the police stationwhere these permits are issued. It is a practical problem. Theyhave to waste their valuable time. It is happening not onlyonce. Even after they show their identity card and the proofof ownership of the vehicle, they have to go through thisprocedure every time when they have to travel to Colomboor elsewhere. So, this is an appeal I make to the Hon. Minister,to consider this. Even the bus drivers who have the routepermit have the same problem. Of coures, they can have theirroutine check wherever. I see elderly people, children andpregnant Iadies have to get down and get in, get down andget in at so many security points. Sometimes, as you know,the security personnel who are also human beings, get irritatedand shout at these people and all that. This is one of thecomplaints we have been continuously receiving from ourpeople. So, you will have to consider this and categorizethem. There are vehicles that are being used by some people,but they are not the owners. You have to have a tight securityon them. They have to obtain a pass each time.

At this juncture, I would also like to bring the the notice ofthe Hon. Ministers concerned regarding the paddy purchasein our area. As you know, the normal life has been disturbedthere. Paddy purchase by the Government is not properlydone, specially in the ampara District. They say there are nostorage facilities. As a result the farmers are suffering. On theone hand the farmers do not have space to stock their paddyand they have to sell paddy lower than the production cost.This is one of the problems the farmers are facing. As a resultalmost 15,000 acres of paddy land is in danger of beingneglected; without cultivation Decisions are taken at thefarmers’ association to this effect. What have they done?During the last three or four seasons, they could not evenrecover their cost of production. So, they have come to astage Where they are not going to cultivate. so, theGovernment has to intervene and provide proper relife, sothat they would be able to continue with their paddycultivation.

ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ

[ªÇæ ¦. ¦. ¦. ÄêÌàºåÀå ÄÍºå]

29212922

There is a complaint from the Oluvil Port workers. This nota time to take political revenge. You know what amount ofdifficulties the people of the Eastern Province are undergoing.If all of a sudden 263 port employees are transferred fromOluvil to Colombo what would be their plight? Their childrenare studying in the schools in that area and the cost of livingis also a factor to be considered. when they come to Colombothey have to rent out rooms as they have to live here inColombo. You cannot get a small room for less then Rs. 5000or Rs. 6000. They have to travel up and down from Oluvil toColombo. How much will it cost? The childern who are aboutto sit for their O/L examination, A/L examination are made tosuffer. So I would appeal to the Minister concerned becausethey say that according to the Letter of Transfer, two hundredand sixty three people are at once transferred. They say thatthey are excess. I understand that there is excess staff in everyport. In Colombo, Trincomalee or Galle everywhere there isexcess staff. But, these workers suspect that there are certainpeople behind this move. This is done on a political basis.So, I do not think these transfers should take place. Theymust cancel it until such time the children of the port workerssit for their examinations, Sir. As you know, the difficulty isthe high cost of living. They cannot meet their expenseswhen they come to Colombo. They have to resign from theirjobs and for something else. The employees who have beentransferred met me and said that the Ministry offered aVoluntary Retirement Scheme to other employees-but not toOulivil port workers -where they were paid compensationand other benefits. But, of course, these Oluvil port workerswere deprived of that opportunity. So if you cannot cancelthese transfers they would like to go on retirement where youhave to pay compensation as you paid for other port workers,Sir. This another complaint. You have to consider the situationnow. Travelling is a problem.

The cost of living is high. they cannot get a room inColombo. Their children’s education is affected. so pleaseconsider the problems faced by the employees of Oluvilport. as you know His Excellency Mahinda Rajapaksa hasinstructed to go ahead with the work at Oluvil port. So youneed more and more people. Do not transfer them and alsoI receive information that a cadre is being created for theMahapola Centre and there is also a housing scheme. Thereare a number of other projects also under ports. You havecreated cadres but they have not considered all that. So youdo not need to transfer these 263 people if you are creating acadre, you can fill there with these people.

Finally, I have to touch on the speeches made by Hon.Sampanthan and the Hon. Rauff Hakeem regarding the de-merger and the request made to the Government. I would saySir, Hon. Rauff Hakeem was in such a position that he couldnot come out with the needs of the Muslim community. Thede-merger, I thank Almighty Allah, was not intiated by aMuslim. Had it been initiated by a Muslim and had a Muslimgone to court and the verdict was this, the Muslims in theEast would have been massacred. There would have been a

bloodbath in the East, Sir Thank God, it had not happened.What we say is that we are against the merger. But, of coursein 1987 without the consent of the Muslims the it was done.What was the result? The Muslim community in the Eastsuffered very much, Sir. so, at this juncture what is the positionof the Muslims? We are not against the merger. But, tell uswhat is our position in the future? In case the two provincesare merged what would be our position? Hon. Rauff Hakeemis talking about a separate non-contiguous administrationcomprising of all the Muslim villages under oneadministration. Not even the LTTE or these Members ofParliament belonging to the TNA have uttered a single wordabout this. So how can you target; how can just go and raiseyour hand in favour or not in favour of the merger? We shouldknow what is position of not only the Muslims but also theposition of the Sinhalese in the East. So until such time, wewould not say, “Yes” or “No” to this. So Hon. Rauff Hakeem,you should reflect the impression of the Muslims. You do notjust come and ask the Government to go ahead. Do notpressurize the Government to take some unwanted decisions.Because of the decision that was taken in 1987, we are stillsuffering. What is happening in the North-East ProvincialCouncil? We, the Muslim community, are being treated as asecondary community. We cannot get anything done. Theresources that are being distributed through the North-EastProvincial Council is not done properly.

ÄìÈåÌ¾åÇç· Ä¾àºòéºëÄå(¶Î¾Îº ¶Ç+ÆÐºÆ §Þ¹Æ¸¼Æ £Á¼Æ¯¿Æ)(The Presiding Member)Hon. Member, your time is over.

ªÇæ ¦. ¦. ¦. ÄêÌàºåÀå ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ©ºÆ° ©ºÆ° ©ºÆ° Û¶¹Ç)(The Hon. M. M. M. Musthaffa)Kindly give me one more minute, Sir. It is not done properly.It is not distributed properly. Even in giving appointments,graduate appointments or the English teaching appointmentsor the nurses’ appointments or minor employees’appointments or whatever appointments, the Muslims arebeing sidelined. They are not considered favourably. So untilsuch time we get the right composition of the administration,until such time they say that this is for the Muslims, this is forthe sinhalese, we do not want to say anything. We do notwant to agree or disagree. You keep it in your mind. We areneither for or against. We would say, “Okay” when it isacceptable to the Muslim community. So at this juncture weare not pressurizing the Government. The Government shouldtake its decision impartially.

I thank you for giving me this opportunity to speak andI wind up.

Subscription : The annual subscription for Official Report of Hansard is Rs. 2,178. A single copy of Hansard is available forRs. 18.15. (Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to theSUPERINTENDENT, GOVERNMENT PUBLICATION BUREAU, No. 32, Transworks House,Lotus Road, Colombo 1. The fee should reach him on or bvefore November 30 each year.Late application for subscriptions will not be accepted.
